  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_0c42101a-de22-49ac-ae96-0ce3347bf75b'
      });
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer15605775476367468876">This beautiful and deeply moving tale recounts educational psychologist Torey Hayden's battle to unlock the emotions of a troubled and sexually abused child who, with the help of Hayden, was finally able to overcome her dark past and realise her full potential. Six-year-old Sheila was abandoned by her mother on a highway when she was four. A survivor of horrific abuse, she</span>
  <span id="freeText15605775476367468876" style="display:none">This beautiful and deeply moving tale recounts educational psychologist Torey Hayden's battle to unlock the emotions of a troubled and sexually abused child who, with the help of Hayden, was finally able to overcome her dark past and realise her full potential. Six-year-old Sheila was abandoned by her mother on a highway when she was four. A survivor of horrific abuse, she never spoke, never cried, and was placed in a class for severely retarded children after committing an atrocious act of violence against another child. Everyone thought Sheila was beyond salvation—except her teacher, Torey Hayden. With patience, skill, and abiding love, she fought long and hard to release a haunted little girl from her secret nightmare—and nurture the spark of genius she recognised trapped within Sheila's silence. This is the remarkable story of their journey together—an odyssey of hope, courage, and inspiring devotion that opened the heart and mind of one lost child to a new world of discovery and joy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15605775476367468876" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_444284660" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/444284660" />
    <a title="Msjess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4951967-msjess"><img alt="Msjess" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1400552791p2/4951967.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/444284660?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Msjess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Msjess" href="/user/show/4951967-msjess">Msjess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789793269061" href="/book/show/1243569.Sheila">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer444284660" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12438485828344663838">I remember reading this story as a child and being engrossed in it. It's reminiscent of "A child called It" because of its extreme depiction of a child in severe abuse and neglect.<br/><br/>Reading again as an adult and as an educator who works with at risk children I was horrified. The story is a memoir written by a special ed teacher. She clearly wants to be praised and lauded for her amazing breakthrough with Sheila but all I could think was that Sheila needed to be put into foster care. She was clearl</span>
  <span id="freeText12438485828344663838" style="display:none">I remember reading this story as a child and being engrossed in it. It's reminiscent of "A child called It" because of its extreme depiction of a child in severe abuse and neglect.<br /><br />Reading again as an adult and as an educator who works with at risk children I was horrified. The story is a memoir written by a special ed teacher. She clearly wants to be praised and lauded for her amazing breakthrough with Sheila but all I could think was that Sheila needed to be put into foster care. She was clearly being abused and neglected, there many warning signs such as the lack of hygiene, her rages, hell the visit to her home. I was baffled as to why Sheila did not seem to be getting any sort of psychological evaluation for hurting the little boy. Even Torey said she didn't want to ask.<br /><br />Worst was when Sheila was sexually assaulted and much is made of how brave Sheila was and how she was so strong...but there was no mention of her getting therapy or being removed from her family's home. At the end it's considered a triumph that she cried because she was remembering her trauma. It wasn't a triumph. It was a sign that she was hurting was going to have a lot of pain to work through.<br /><br />I have not read the equal but apparently in it Torey tracks Sheila down because her book has been a success and readers were clamoring for a sequel, not because she actually wanted to see how Sheila was doing. And worse she seemed upset that Sheila was mad at her instead of grateful. I don't blame Sheila at all for being mad at Torey for failing to do the right thing as a mandatory reporter and as a human being.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12438485828344663838" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Kat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/105191338-kat"><img alt="Kat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573354185p2/105191338.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        <a title="Kat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat" href="/user/show/105191338-kat">Kat</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36694745-one-child">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/105191338-kat?shelf=power-dynamics">power-dynamics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/105191338-kat?shelf=parent-child-relationships">parent-child-relationships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/105191338-kat?shelf=trauma">trauma</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/105191338-kat?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/105191338-kat?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3414467496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13783955680190500420">This true story chronicles the experiences of the author, Torey Hayden, a special education teacher at the time, and a very troubled, yet gifted 6-year old girl named Sheila who was placed in her small class of kids with varying degrees of disability. Sheila was put there by the courts as a temporary placement while awaiting an opening in the children’s unit of the state mental hospital - a result of her unprovoked and serious attack on a 3-year old boy. What follows is the journey of discovery </span>
  <span id="freeText13783955680190500420" style="display:none">This true story chronicles the experiences of the author, Torey Hayden, a special education teacher at the time, and a very troubled, yet gifted 6-year old girl named Sheila who was placed in her small class of kids with varying degrees of disability. Sheila was put there by the courts as a temporary placement while awaiting an opening in the children’s unit of the state mental hospital - a result of her unprovoked and serious attack on a 3-year old boy. What follows is the journey of discovery over the 5 months Hayden worked with her, that this little girl wasn’t a monster in need of caging, but a child who’d experienced a highly traumatic background and was struggling to cope with it. It was also discovered that she was extremely intelligent, which further convinced Hayden that the course being set for the child by the system wasn’t appropriate and should be fought. <br /><br />Hayden’s efforts to bring Sheila out of her personal darkness and form a trusting relationship with her and her peers is the basis of the book. Watching Torey and Sheila navigate their way into each others' lives and hearts is truly special, and in turns both uplifting and heart-breaking. I work with children Sheila’s age, so this one particularly hit me in the heart. Reading about a child’s trauma is hard. What I appreciated, though, is that it’s a very human book. We see Sheila at her worst, but we also see those moments of breakthrough, where all you want is for her to succeed and have a happy life. Hayden isn’t a saint, and she struggles with her own frustration of trying to reach the girl, but I can only admire her commitment and efforts to reach a child most people would have given up on. It’s a tough, but rewarding and insightful read. I will warn, though, not to expect a clear-cut resolution to the story. This book was published in 1980, and Hayden wrote a 1995 sequel: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30840376.The_Tiger_s_Child_What_Ever_Happened_to_Sheila_" title="The Tiger's Child What Ever Happened to Sheila? by Torey L. Hayden" rel="nofollow noopener">The Tiger's Child: What Ever Happened to Sheila?</a> that answers some of those questions. My review for that: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3414954133" rel="nofollow noopener">The Tiger's Child</a><br /> <br />★★★★ Stars<br /><br />******************************************************************************************************************************************************************************<br /><br />SPOILER: THE FOLLOWING TRIGGER WARNING REVEALS A MAJOR EVENT IN THE BOOK<br /><br />There is an instance related by the author of severe child sexual abuse and the after effects that may be very upsetting to some. If that is a problem for you, you should avoid the book</span>
  <a data-text-id="13783955680190500420" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1089427299" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1089427299" />
    <a title="Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6665735-books"><img alt="Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419956881p2/6665735.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1089427299?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Books" href="/user/show/6665735-books">Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9788863803" href="/book/show/23251657-one-child">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1089427299" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer676217390047938595">The first thing I want to tell you is how much this book made me cry. Buckets full. Maybe even enough to fill an ocean. Ugly cry, even. Unashamed, let-it-all-out, bawling. That’s how much. I’m not even exaggerating. This is significant, because tearjerker movies get me to cry often, but in contrast, only a handful of books have managed to dissolve me into tears. With One Child, I cried often, and I cried long and hard. It’s not only Sheila’s circumstances that made me cry, but also because I was</span>
  <span id="freeText676217390047938595" style="display:none">The first thing I want to tell you is how much this book made me cry. Buckets full. Maybe even enough to fill an ocean. Ugly cry, even. Unashamed, let-it-all-out, bawling. That’s how much. I’m not even exaggerating. This is significant, because tearjerker movies get me to cry often, but in contrast, only a handful of books have managed to dissolve me into tears. With One Child, I cried often, and I cried long and hard. It’s not only Sheila’s circumstances that made me cry, but also because I was so grateful that there is a teacher who cared enough to save this little girl whom everyone had given up on. <br /><br />Let me share a little about Sheila. She is a six-year-old girl who committed a terrible crime. It wasn’t her first crime, but it was probably her worst. At the age of six she had already had run ins with the police three times, and after her last crime the courts had decided that she should be placed in a state institution for mentally disturbed patients. Unfortunately for the state, but fortunately for Sheila, there wasn’t space available to accommodate her in the local state institution, and she was placed in a classroom for handicapped, abused, and mentally disturbed children. The teacher for that classroom at the time was Miss Torey (the author of this book). According to state regulations, Torey could only accommodate eight children in her classroom due to the severity of their conditions. Yet, she had no choice but to accept problem-child Sheila into her classroom.<br /><br />When I say Sheila is a problem-child, I don’t mean it lightly. The things she does is incredibly shocking, but here I also want to mention that she is no ordinary child. She has an IQ of over 170. Obviously, until Sheila has landed in Torey’s classroom, no-one has figured it out yet because Sheila is such a difficult child who goes out of her way to make herself unlovable. She lives in poverty with her alcoholic, ex-convict father, in a one-room shack in a migrant camp. You might wonder where Sheila’s mother is, and I can only tell you that that is another heartbreaking part of Sheila’s life. No acceptable excuse can be made for what Sheila’s mother did to her. It’s just too appalling. <br /><br />Anyway, the entire story centers around Miss Torey and Sheila forming an unbreakable bond and how they changed each others’ lives, and also how it changed Sheila. This little girl who never cries and who only knows rejection, abuse, and abandonment, has to learn to love, be accepted, deal with her anger, and adjust to normal society - what is socially acceptable, and what is not. Often I found myself smiling about how Sheila perceives the world and her surroundings, and how she tries to make sense of her life. The other kids in the same classroom also crept into my heart. So many times did I go “aaawwwhhh” because of something or other that Sheila, Torey or any of the other kids did or say, and then the tears would start all over again.<br /><br />I’ve read many abuse stories, whether it’s written in books or news articles, but never have I been as shocked as when I read what Sheila’s uncle did to her. You think you’ve heard it all with regard to the extent of human depravity, and then you read something like that... <br /><br />The story has a good ending, but not, in my opinion, a satisfying one. I desperately wanted a different ending for Sheila at home. I didn’t agree with the welfare system’s opinion of Sheila’s home life. I appreciated every single effort Torey made to improve Sheila’s life and I am grateful that there are teachers who really care about their students. One Child is a book worth reading, albeit not an easy one because it plays havoc with your emotions. Whether this really happened or not, it is a reminder that the world is filled with people who have no limits to the cruelties they bestow on defenseless little children (and animals, for that matter). At the same time it also showcases that, once in a while, a gem such as Torey comes along who dedicates her time and all of herself to protecting, loving, and making a difference in the lives of little ones who can’t fend for themselves. <br /><br />As much as I want to recommend this book to everyone, I also have to issue a warning that it contains content of a disturbing nature. Sheila’s story needed to be told and I’m grateful to Ms Hayden for sharing it with us. However, read it at own risk (such as crying buckets of tears and having your heart break into tiny little pieces over and over again). <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="676217390047938595" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6250843915026305072" style="display:none">This book is about a special ed teacher and her relationship with "one child". The child, Sheila, has been severely abused, left on the interstate by her mother, neglected by her father and is only 6 years old. The story is a true store of how Hayden helped Sheila come out of her shell and trust someone will not abandon her and begin to love again.<br /><br />I liked the story, however, the teacher/author, Hayden annoyed me. I felt she made herself into a hero, and very few teachers could be like her and endure what she had to. She tended to justify EVERYTHING she did, right or wrong. She is a good story teller but thinks entirely too much of herself, in my opinion.<br /><br />I am curious whatever happened to little Sheila. Her story is heartbreaking...</span>

  <span id="freeText14970025331608818973" style="display:none">I’ve been a Torey Hayden fan for decades and am delighted to rediscover her books in Kindle version as my eyes focus better on ebooks thanks to cataracts and age. Fixed the cataracts, age not so much. I’ve read her books multiple times over the years. I can’t say they directly influenced my decision to become a child psychologist, but Torey planted seeds of interest in being able to help children improve their ability to cope with psychological challenges.<br /><br />Hayden has worked as an educator for emotionally disturbed children in various settings. ONE CHILD is the story of Sheila, an abused, neglected and angry child whose behavior challenges the ever patient Hayden. In TIGER’S EYE, a follow up book written years later, Torey finds Sheila as a teen and we see what’s happened since and the limitations of Hayden’s ability to help Sheila.<br /><br />A huge recommendation for this and all Hayden’s books.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2324348599" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2324348599" />
    <a title="Glen Grunau" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2499125-glen-grunau"><img alt="Glen Grunau" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360207033p2/2499125.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2324348599?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Glen Grunau" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Glen Grunau" href="/user/show/2499125-glen-grunau">Glen Grunau</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/18516457-one-child">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2324348599" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14003129074528258753">I am not prone to crying at movies or books but this simple story had me in tears on several occasions. <br/><br/>This story was from a different era. When the child welfare system was ill equipped to deal with child abuse and children known to be suffering from severe neglect were left in horrific conditions. There were not enough social workers, foster homes, or welfare checks to go around. When child trauma and reactive attachment was managed by professionals with authoritative and controlling practice</span>
  <span id="freeText14003129074528258753" style="display:none">I am not prone to crying at movies or books but this simple story had me in tears on several occasions. <br /><br />This story was from a different era. When the child welfare system was ill equipped to deal with child abuse and children known to be suffering from severe neglect were left in horrific conditions. There were not enough social workers, foster homes, or welfare checks to go around. When child trauma and reactive attachment was managed by professionals with authoritative and controlling practices. If children like Sheila were to have a chance, then they needed someone like Torey Hayden to go beyond duty and offer the embrace of love. <br /><br />Which begs the question: Is human indifference sometimes the result of having a better equipped (although still so far from perfect) child welfare system? It is so easy just to call the social worker when we observe child abuse and neglect and feel like this is all that is required of us.<br /><br />I recall my first job interview after my undergraduate degree. It was at Browndale Group Homes in Burnaby. Their prescribed treatment for kids with attachment disorder was prolonged and unremitting physical restraint - until all of the anger and fear and emotion of the child was bled out of them. Soon thereafter this "holding" fell out of favour as the research and treatment of attachment disorder evolved. <br /><br />A story from my own work with children, that happened one year after this book was written. My first post-degree job included my assignment as a youth care worker to a boy named Jeff. He and his single mother loved in poverty in a small trailer in Burnaby. I did not know his story, only that he and his mother were under the watchful eye of child welfare. My time with Jeff was short-lived as I soon moved on to a different job. My only clear recollection of my time with him was the visit I had with him and his mother in their small trailer . . . and the time I was meeting with his school teacher in a classroom and looked out the window to see Jeff jumping out of my VW after releasing the handbrake. I could see my car starting to roll down the hill. Running at full speed I still could not catch up and thankfully some alert motorist drove in front of my vehicle and was able to bring both cars to a stop after until my car nudged up against his. <br /><br />One Child illustrates how the compassion and love and unwavering dedication of one educator was transformative in the life of a highly disturbed and "unreachable" 6 year old child. The power was in the story; there was nothing spectacular in how it was written. But it was honestly written. I appreciated the vulnerabiity of the author when she chose to include her own weaker moments and failed attempts. I was grateful for her compassion to recognize that in the life of every victimizer there is a victim. <br /><br />How to explain my own emotional reaction to the book? Good stories about vulnerable children, whether in a novel or on the movie screen, always seem to touch me more most deeply. Maybe this is related to a story of Jesus. Once his friends were upset because Jesus was spending time with little children when he had important adults to teach. Something about his response tells me that we need to pay close attention to what children can teach us: “Let the children come to me. Don’t stop them! For the Kingdom of Heaven belongs to those who are like these children.”<br /><br />If you have read this book, you might be interested in this "where are they now" follow-up: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.torey-hayden.com/one_child.htm">http://www.torey-hayden.com/one_child...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14003129074528258753" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="Ruth Turner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ruth Turner" href="/user/show/17861817-ruth-turner">Ruth Turner</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007199051" href="/book/show/76377.One_Child">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17861817-ruth-turner?shelf=memoir-autobiography-biography">memoir-autobiography-biography</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer901485077&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer901485077" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16415938478864827022"><br/><br/>It's so difficult to rate and review true books about child abuse, and this one is no exception.<br/><br/>Well written, easy to read and a cast of delightful characters. Especially the "crazy kidses." I loved them.<br/><br/>However, there was one thing about this book that I have to mention because it affected my overall view of the story. <br/><br/>Sheila, six years old and the main character of the story, is sexually abused by her uncle. When he tried to have sex with her she was too small, so he cut her with a knife. Tore</span>
  <span id="freeText16415938478864827022" style="display:none"><br /><br />It's so difficult to rate and review true books about child abuse, and this one is no exception.<br /><br />Well written, easy to read and a cast of delightful characters. Especially the "crazy kidses." I loved them.<br /><br />However, there was one thing about this book that I have to mention because it affected my overall view of the story. <br /><br />Sheila, six years old and the main character of the story, is sexually abused by her uncle. When he tried to have sex with her she was too small, so he cut her with a knife. Torey, her teacher, has to explain what happened to the other children in her class. These are special needs children, mentally, emotionally and physically disadvantaged and they were worried about their friend who was bleeding when she came to school and then rushed to hospital.<br /><br />"Remember I told you that Sheila got hurt at<br />home. And remember back when we were<br />talking about the ways people can touch<br />you? I was telling you how sometimes<br />people want to put their hands places on a<br />little kid's body that they have no right to<br />touch."<br /><br />"Yeah, like down where it's private on you,<br />huh?" said William.<br /><br />I nodded. "Well, someone in Sheila's family<br />touched her where he shouldn't have and<br />when Sheila got unhappy about it, he hurt<br />her."<br /><br />Foreheads wrinkled. Their eyes were intent.<br />Even Max stopped rocking.<br /><br />"What did he do to her?" William asked.<br /><br />"Cut her."<br /><br />The children thought they were old enough to be told the truth, so that's what she gave them. She does speculate on whether she's done the right thing in being so honest, and decides that she has.<br /><br />This horrified me so much that I almost didn't finish the book. There's truth and there's truth, and I think I'd struggle with any children being given this much information, let alone a group of special needs kiddies.<br /><br />I think it will be quite some time before I read another of her books.<br /><br />*climbs down off soap box* <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16415938478864827022" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText5861289620449771099" style="display:none">ahh. One Child, by Torey Hayden was just plain... FANTASTIC... AMAZING... GREAT... I LOVED the book. It was about a young girl at the age of 5 years old is what I remember. Okay, so she was left on the side of a highway hanging on the gate by her mother, which left her to go live in California with the little girls' only and little brother. Her dad found her and took her back home, where she always gets abused and is taught many things. <br /><br />So when she goes to school, she has the knowledge of a 5th grader. BUT she has the behavior of a 2 year old. She screams, and hurts children and interrupts the class. But thank God for the teacher. <br /><br />Her teacher, Torey Hayden is a person who helps special or tortured children in their life. For example, Sheila! She calms them down and what-so-ever. Her and Sheilas' relationship is so bad at first. But then as the book goes on Torey calms Sheila down and become like best friends. <br /><br />I really loved the book. It taught such a great lesson and I would read this book, also, again later in my life. I would recommend this book to many people. Well like, EVERYONE because of how much I loved it. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14781546280631275462">Torey Hayden is a teacher of those children society deems "garbage"...autistic, schizophrenic, emotionally damaged, suicidal. This was in the seventies and eighties, before autism became a popular disease. I read One Child, a book I've read before, which the story of Sheila, a six year old so abused and emotionally scarred that she takes a neighborhood child out to the woods and sets fire to him. Because no one else will take her into a normal classroom, Torey gets her. She's emaciated, owns one</span>
  <span id="freeText14781546280631275462" style="display:none">Torey Hayden is a teacher of those children society deems "garbage"...autistic, schizophrenic, emotionally damaged, suicidal. This was in the seventies and eighties, before autism became a popular disease. I read One Child, a book I've read before, which the story of Sheila, a six year old so abused and emotionally scarred that she takes a neighborhood child out to the woods and sets fire to him. Because no one else will take her into a normal classroom, Torey gets her. She's emaciated, owns one shirt and one filthy pair of overalls, and reeks because she wets the bed every night and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1812457.The_Shack" title="The Shack by William P. Young" rel="nofollow noopener">the shack</a> she and her father live in has no running water for bathing. In one shocking scene, she gouges out the eyes of the classroom goldfish and strangles the baby gerbils that belong to one of the teacher's sons. Reading her books actually lit a fire in my oldest daughter to work with autistic children, and not only does she tutor an autistic second-grader in our school, but is headed off to college in the fall for a degree in Special Education. If you love children, read these books. But have the Kleenex ready.<br /><br /></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/436516216?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ReaderSP" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ReaderSP" href="/user/show/13729798-readersp">ReaderSP</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer436516216" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18378211813734995471">I have read a few of Torey Hayden's books and I had been meaning to read this one for a long time. A usually with Hayden's books, it follows her experiences working with children with special needs and running a special needs class. The main character in the book is Shelia, a very troubled young girl. Shelia comes to Hayden's class at the age of 7, whilst waiting for a placement in a secure unit, after committing a horrible crime on another child. Shelia is a disruptive mute, whose worse attribu</span>
  <span id="freeText18378211813734995471" style="display:none">I have read a few of Torey Hayden's books and I had been meaning to read this one for a long time. A usually with Hayden's books, it follows her experiences working with children with special needs and running a special needs class. The main character in the book is Shelia, a very troubled young girl. Shelia comes to Hayden's class at the age of 7, whilst waiting for a placement in a secure unit, after committing a horrible crime on another child. Shelia is a disruptive mute, whose worse attribute is her anger. Given all that, Shelia is a girl everyone wants to know and help. Although Shelia has experienced things we could not imagine in her short life, she is still strong and carries such charm and innocence. You get to know and feel for her and her father, who has issues of his own. Simple things like cleaning and feeding Shelia never really happen and Hayden show Shelia how to look after herself. Just as things are getting better for Shelia, something happens and she is transported back to square one. You really feel for this small, little girl and your heart breaks at her story. This book is packed with emotion and you will not be able to put it down. I'm off to read the sequel Tiger's Child.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18378211813734995471" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5599085333028617352">Great book. <br/>This book follows the progress of a child that was placed in Ms. Hayden's classroom because there was 'no where else to put her' as she waited for an opening at the state hospital.<br/>I felt this book was sincerely written, and very honest. It didn't dance around the subject matter at all. I also felt that Ms. Hayden was writing from a fairly objective perspective. She didn't toot her own horn constantly, nor did she degrade or downplay the roles of others in the process of working with </span>
  <span id="freeText5599085333028617352" style="display:none">Great book. <br />This book follows the progress of a child that was placed in Ms. Hayden's classroom because there was 'no where else to put her' as she waited for an opening at the state hospital.<br />I felt this book was sincerely written, and very honest. It didn't dance around the subject matter at all. I also felt that Ms. Hayden was writing from a fairly objective perspective. She didn't toot her own horn constantly, nor did she degrade or downplay the roles of others in the process of working with this girl. <br />This book would be a great read for anyone who has contemplated, or is contemplating, working in a resource style classroom setting. As well as those who have, are currently, or would like to work with children through the social welfare system, as a resource teacher, or even a psychologist. <br />Highly recommended. <br /><br />Also note there is a follow up book to this one called "Tiger Child" (or something like that) that I cannot wait to find and read. In fact, I would be happy to read any of Ms. Hayden's books, and there are several out there.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15319773668803507193">This book was absorbing and enthralling. It drew me in slowly, introducing Sheila, first, as merely a statistic in a newspaper. Insignificant and unimportant despite the horrendous act which she has committed. This is a good way for us to "meet" this brilliant and joyous little girl because it's how she has been viewed all of her short life. We are told in brutal honesty about Sheila's early life and her upbringing. At 6 she has experiences things a grown adult could barely comprehend but she is</span>
  <span id="freeText15319773668803507193" style="display:none">This book was absorbing and enthralling. It drew me in slowly, introducing Sheila, first, as merely a statistic in a newspaper. Insignificant and unimportant despite the horrendous act which she has committed. This is a good way for us to "meet" this brilliant and joyous little girl because it's how she has been viewed all of her short life. We are told in brutal honesty about Sheila's early life and her upbringing. At 6 she has experiences things a grown adult could barely comprehend but she is found to be something of a genius. Torey Hayden is an extraordinary teacher and a beautiful person with a good heart. She loves and cares about Sheila, and all of "her" children and this is conveyed so strongly that the reader cannot help but invest their emotions and love them too. This book brought tears, bursts of anger, and a few little smiles and giggles. Not for the faint hearted, because Sheila is one amazing 6 year old and if you're not quite as brave and as strong as she, you may not make it to the last page. </span>

  <span id="freeText15361647309495186596" style="display:none">THIS IS FOR "ONE CHILD" ONLY I first formed my relationship with Sheila in the 5th grade as part of an advanced English class. I remember thinking oh my gosh this really happened to such a brilliant child. Sheila was a 5 yr old child who lived in such horrific circumstances that the rats round her had better lives. She is considered helpless after she sets a 3yr old on fire. No where to go the State puts her in a special education classroom. There she meets Torey a teacher, who helps Sheila blossom into a child that you can't help fall in love with. Torey Hayden will put you into the mind of this child and have you engaging in very raw emotions. I fell in love with this book when I was 11 yrs old and as I reread it this year, I will say the complexity of mental disorders and the people who treat this amazes me. I admire Mrs Hayden for her patience and her ability to help so many children. This book is powerful and emotionally gripping.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007821112" href="/book/show/21239533-one-child">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer558330258" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5541622160052350204">One of my most loved books of all time. I read it many times as a teenager and in my 20's until I lost track of my copy. Finally picked up a new copy, and it was like being reunited with an old friend. Torey Hayden's One Child was the first book I ever read about behaviorally challenged children. I loved it so much back then, that I eagerly went off in search of her other titles, and eventually branched out into other teacher-authors (like Mary MacCracken). There are now many titles in this cate</span>
  <span id="freeText5541622160052350204" style="display:none">One of my most loved books of all time. I read it many times as a teenager and in my 20's until I lost track of my copy. Finally picked up a new copy, and it was like being reunited with an old friend. Torey Hayden's One Child was the first book I ever read about behaviorally challenged children. I loved it so much back then, that I eagerly went off in search of her other titles, and eventually branched out into other teacher-authors (like Mary MacCracken). There are now many titles in this category that are on my "you've-got-to-read-this" list! <br />But, One Child was the book that started it all for me. If you love children, and you believe all people are inherently good and deserving of care and affection, then you will enjoy this book! I have no doubt you will also set out to read her other titles after you tearfully finish this read. Miss Hayden proves that love really is the strongest force on earth.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5541622160052350204" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I wasn't sure if I was going to like it or how I would feel about it, but I have to say I was pleasantly surprised. The book was great, it was written beautifully and in good taste. I enjoyed reading this book and will most defiantly being reading the follow up books and other books by Torey Hayden in the future. Very glad I read it. 5/5 </span>

<div id="review_3598943391" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3598943391" />
    <a title="lucy  Ü " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/92065625-lucy"><img alt="lucy  Ü " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597166545p2/92065625.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3598943391?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="lucy  Ü " class="user" itemprop="url" name="lucy  Ü " href="/user/show/92065625-lucy">lucy  Ü </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3598943391" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16342593240872854190">This book definitely was not an easy read. There's moments where you're like "Okay, things are getting better now..." and then something completely awful happens and you're like "no. no. no. no. no." and you kinda need to close your eyes for a bit. <br/><br/>but emotional disturbance is real and it's plaguing far more children than it should. i always find myself asking "why?" and "how?" as a teacher. Why do people choose to abuse (emotionally, physically, and/or sexually) children? How can we stop this? </span>
  <span id="freeText16342593240872854190" style="display:none">This book definitely was not an easy read. There's moments where you're like "Okay, things are getting better now..." and then something completely awful happens and you're like "no. no. no. no. no." and you kinda need to close your eyes for a bit. <br /><br />but emotional disturbance is real and it's plaguing far more children than it should. i always find myself asking "why?" and "how?" as a teacher. Why do people choose to abuse (emotionally, physically, and/or sexually) children? How can we stop this? Why does this continue to plague our world? Why isn't anybody talking about this reality. <br /><br />The fact that Sheila was a real girl who really suffered is heart-shattering. I want to just scoop that girl into my arms and tell her that in all the bad, there is still good. It pains my heart knowing that there are so many children who deal with this kind of trauma every single day and sometimes I don't know what to do. But that's why I became a teacher - so I can make a difference like Torey did for Sheila. <br /><br />This book will wreck you. Just like the memoir <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2043412.Hope_s_Boy_A_Memoir" title="Hope's Boy A Memoir by Andrew Bridge" rel="nofollow noopener">Hope's Boy: A Memoir</a> it will open your eyes and shock you a bit - but that's the point. We need to be aware of these children and we need to be aware that they need help.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_129194747" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/129194747" />
    <a title="Kara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/105003-kara"><img alt="Kara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1180492592p2/105003.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/129194747?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kara" href="/user/show/105003-kara">Kara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/18516457-one-child">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/105003-kara?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/105003-kara?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129194747" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12601178965301867727">I purposefully read this book directly after "The Boy Who Was Raised As a Dog: And Other Stories from a Child Psychiatrist's Notebook: What Traumatized Children Can Teach Us About Loss, Love and Healing" by Bruce Perry, which came out in 2007. Hayden's book was published in 1980, and it was a very different world then in education, especially when it came to children with special needs or histories of abuse, neglect, trauma, or unstable backgrounds. In a world where abused children could be take</span>
  <span id="freeText12601178965301867727" style="display:none">I purposefully read this book directly after "The Boy Who Was Raised As a Dog: And Other Stories from a Child Psychiatrist's Notebook: What Traumatized Children Can Teach Us About Loss, Love and Healing" by Bruce Perry, which came out in 2007. Hayden's book was published in 1980, and it was a very different world then in education, especially when it came to children with special needs or histories of abuse, neglect, trauma, or unstable backgrounds. In a world where abused children could be taken to the principal's office to be paddled or all be lumped together no matter what type of "crazy" they were: autistic, blind, behavioral problems (no matter what the cause). What amazes me is that Hayden, without all the brain research to back her up, had to resort to her own methods to do what she could for children like Sheila. And while sometimes her methods might seem like going against what is now considered common practice... she got results. Hayden had to follow her own heart, mind, and gut feelings paired with her experience and natural ability to reach out to children with whom she would have no or little support from the educational system. Sometimes my heart would ache for Sheila, and for Hayden who had so little of a support system in what must have been completely emotionally draining, and incredibly unrewarding at times. And yet what she accomplishes in Sheila's life is amazing and commendable. <br /><br />I had read this book over and over again since about middle school. Now that I am a teacher with an understanding of development and students of my own who test me in their own ways, rereading it brought this story into a whole new life. It is a quick, easy read that draws you in immediately, and well flowing. At first the first person narrative threw me off because it is a memoir, and often I wondered how Hayden was reiterating exact conversations and how much had been changed, either over time or by affected emotional memories. But it doesn't take away from what is indeed a touching story where you simply can't help but root for Sheila and Torey-- in fact, the fact that Hayden is so much a part of this story only strengthens the books emotional appeal. I know there is a followup book on Sheila that I'd like to read, but I also hope that it might give a clue as to what happened in the lives of some of the other characters-- the other children in her class, or Anton and Whitney: Hayden makes you not just involved in her life or Sheila's, but all the other people who were also such a huge part of her life.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12601178965301867727" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2606306496" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2606306496" />
    <a title="Nora Cassandra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7693904-nora-cassandra"><img alt="Nora Cassandra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523864363p2/7693904.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2606306496?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nora Cassandra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nora Cassandra" href="/user/show/7693904-nora-cassandra">Nora Cassandra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007240630" href="/book/show/1159749.One_Child">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2606306496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2963862624211486656">I read this book for psychology essay. I read reviews before reading so I was pulled back at first. So My advice just grab the book read it then think for yourself. <br/><br/>It was a good book for a study case. I do admit getting emotional in many parts. I had to stop and take a short break. But as I had to read it really fast I couldn't afford big breaks. Do approach with caution as it is graphic, full of trauma and abuse.<br/><br/>The book was well written and NO I don't think Torey is trying to take any credit </span>
  <span id="freeText2963862624211486656" style="display:none">I read this book for psychology essay. I read reviews before reading so I was pulled back at first. So My advice just grab the book read it then think for yourself. <br /><br />It was a good book for a study case. I do admit getting emotional in many parts. I had to stop and take a short break. But as I had to read it really fast I couldn't afford big breaks. Do approach with caution as it is graphic, full of trauma and abuse.<br /><br />The book was well written and NO I don't think Torey is trying to take any credit in the book. Remember the events in the book take place very early 70s, where getting spanked for mistakes was not a child abuse. Torey also talks about her own mistakes with this case so she just looks like a human being nothing more.<br /><br />If researching about trauma, child abuse effects, psychology or to become a teacher I would highly recommend this book.<br /><br />Because of this book I went and got other 4 books for Torey to read. Can't wait.</span>

          </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78139788?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carolyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="carolyn" href="/user/show/69788-carolyn">carolyn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780380542628" href="/book/show/884295.One_Child">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78139788" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17232300319896388349">This book is about a young girl, abused in so many ways, and thanks to a wonderful teacher (one who actually cares about the children she works with, versus those who are there for whatever reason). This child overcomes more in her early years of life than what most people do in a life time. My hats off to Torey Hayden; for the love, strength, and hope that she has given to this child..... and to "Sheila" for gaining the trust in someone to show her that people do care and that there are actuall</span>
  <span id="freeText17232300319896388349" style="display:none">This book is about a young girl, abused in so many ways, and thanks to a wonderful teacher (one who actually cares about the children she works with, versus those who are there for whatever reason). This child overcomes more in her early years of life than what most people do in a life time. My hats off to Torey Hayden; for the love, strength, and hope that she has given to this child..... and to "Sheila" for gaining the trust in someone to show her that people do care and that there are actually good loving people in the world. An awesome story of love, strength, and over coming. I would recommend this book to all. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17232300319896388349" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_10918089'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10918089-one-child-by-torey-hayden-summary-study-guide"><img alt="One Child by Torey Hayden Summary &amp; Study Guide" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1442876348l/10918089._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vIUCuMrNF6e4pGqRxl2pNNMr+MZEq5uxda+f0eiXeSv9moMwQ63vc68z1oOUzufeJu5eMvvng1x7QCA961NavQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BtFByNkOrbmyWf81SRPqvIOUbp1O9R30ULHo5onfqbFHzsBAUG5VbaXOQycbgKRWdlHIafG5BRleXlcKihuKJw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3039876626936088196"><b>Victoria Lynn Hayden</b>, known as <b>Torey L. Hayden</b> (born May 21, 1951 in Livingston, Montana) is a child psychologist, special education teacher, university lecturer and writer of non-fiction books based on her real-life experiences with teaching and counselling children with special needs.<br/>Subjects covered in her books include autism, Tourette syndrome, sexual abuse, fetal alcohol syndrome, and electi</span>
  <span id="freeText3039876626936088196" style="display:none"><b>Victoria Lynn Hayden</b>, known as <b>Torey L. Hayden</b> (born May 21, 1951 in Livingston, Montana) is a child psychologist, special education teacher, university lecturer and writer of non-fiction books based on her real-life experiences with teaching and counselling children with special needs.<br />Subjects covered in her books include autism, Tourette syndrome, sexual abuse, fetal alcohol syndrome, and elective mutism (now called selective mutism), her specialty.<br />Hayden attended high school in Billings, Montana and graduated in 1969. She then attended Whitman College in Walla Walla, Washington.<br />A little time after having written her most famous book One Child, Hayden moved to Wales in 1980 and got married to a Scot called Ken two years later. In 1985, she gave birth to her daughter Sheena. Hayden is now divorced.<br />She has also written three books of fiction in addition to her non-fiction books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3039876626936088196" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
